The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺): IDAs are widely used for selective and sensitive detection of metal cations, often through colorimetric or fluorescent changes.\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, fluoride, chloride): Many IDAs are designed to detect specific anions by exploiting their binding affinities to the host.\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, drugs): IDAs can be tailored to recognize small biomolecules or pharmaceuticals, especially those with functional groups that interact with the host.\n- Biomacromolecules (e.g., proteins, nucleic acids): With appropriate design, IDAs can be used to detect larger biological molecules, though this is less common than for small molecules and ions.\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the modularity of the host and indicator components, allowing for the detection of a broad spectrum of analytes by tuning the host's binding properties. The key requirement is that the target molecule must be able to displace the indicator from the host, resulting in a measurable signal change.", 'key_concepts': ['indicator_displacement_assay (IDA)', The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺): IDAs are widely used for selective and sensitive detection of metal cations, often through colorimetric or fluorescent changes.\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, fluoride, chloride): Many IDAs are designed to detect specific anions by exploiting their binding affinities to the host.\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, drugs): IDAs can be tailored to recognize small biomolecules or pharmaceuticals, especially those with functional groups that interact with the host.\n- Biomacromolecules (e.g., proteins, nucleic acids): With appropriate design, IDAs can be used to detect larger biological molecules, though this is less common than for small molecules and ions.\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the modularity of the host and indicator components, allowing for the detection of a broad spectrum of analytes by tuning the host's binding properties.
